Let's analyze more systematically. The game is a two-player game with perfect information. We can try to find a "strategy" for one player that ensures that the opponent eventually cannot move. This is reminiscent of a "pursuit" game where the "resource" is the sum and sum of squares. Possibly we can consider the "critical" λ where the "average" of the squares constraint is exactly the sum constraint. Since the game is infinite, we can consider the "limiting" behavior. Suppose both players play optimally. Let's try to find a "potential" function that is monotonic and bounded. Define the "state" as (S, Q). The game proceeds with alternating moves. We can think of the game as a "two-player" game where each player tries to force the other to violate the bound. This is similar to a "game of 'tug of war'" where each player can "spend" a resource to increase the cost for the opponent.
